Prophetic Truthfulness Proven by Moral Conduct
Sanusi proves prophetic truthfulness from their moral character and endurance of harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the prophets' moral character and selfless endurance serve as a proof of their truthfulness, independent of miracles.

Core Idea
The prophets' conduct itself proves they are truthful.

Sanusi presents a compelling argument that does not rely on miracles: the very character and sacrifices of the prophets demonstrate their truthfulness. By examining their asceticism, humility, compassion, and patience under persecution, we see a coherence that cannot coexist with deception. This lesson explores that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm and the list of qualities come through.
Notice the extensive list of virtues and the vivid description of the Prophet's suffering.
2
Identify the moral qualities
List the attributes Sanusi mentions: commitment to truth, asceticism, humility, compassion, sincerity, fear of God, equality in calling, forbearance, and selfless endurance.
These are not random; they form a coherent picture.
3
Understand the qarina concept
Sanusi says the qarina (circumstantial evidence) of their state precludes lying. Reflect on how the cumulative evidence of their lives makes deception impossible.
The qarina is the overall pattern, not just one virtue.
4
Connect to the conclusion
The passage concludes that these qualities 'by their mere self' indicate truthfulness. Ask yourself: why would a liar live this way?
The argument is built on coherence and self-consistency.
5
Reflect on the proof's independence
This proof works without miracles. Consider its strength for someone who might doubt miracle reports.
Sanusi provides a rational moral argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليهم الصلاةُ السلامُ التزامُ الصِّدْقِ ، ورفع الهمَّةِ عن كل دناءة ، والزهد في الدنيا بأسرها ؛ بحيث استوى عندهم ذهبُها ومدرُها ، والتزامُ غـايـة الـتـواضـع مـعَ الفقراء والمساكين ، وإسقاط الجاه والمنزلة عندَ الخَلْقِ ، وطلبها عند الملكِ الحقِّ ، وعظيم ما جُبلوا عليهِ مِنَ الشفقة على المخلوقين ، والنصحُ التام لعبادِ اللهِ تعالى ، وكثرةُ جميع الخوفِ منه جلَّ وعزَّ ، والمبادرة لامتثالِ ما بَلَّغوا عنه قبل كلّ أحدٍ ، والمواظبة إلى المماتِ على دعاءِ الخَلْقِ إِلى اللهِ تعالى ، مع التسوية في ذلكَ بين وضيعهم ورفيعهم ، وغنيهم وفقيرهم ، وفطينهم وبليدهم ، وأعجمهم وفصيحهم، وحُرِّهم وعبدِهم، وذكرهم وأنثاهم . وحاضرهم وغائبهم ، وملكهم وسوقتِهم ثم سعة الصدور لحمل سوء إيذائهم وشدَّةِ جفائهم والرأفة على جميعِهم أكثرَ مِنْ رأفتِهم على أولادهم بل وعلى أنفسهم ، مِنْ غيرِ عوض يأخذونه منهم ، ولا منفعة دنيوية تحصل لهم مِنْ قِبَلِهم ، بل هم عليهم الصلاة والسلام تعرَّضوا بذلك لشدائد وأهوال نالتهم مِنْ جهتِهم ، لا يثبتُ لها إلا مَنْ هو على صميم الحقِّ ، قد شغلَهُ التلذذ برضا مولاه ، عن أن يستعظم شيئاً يوصله إلى مرادِهِ منه ومناه وقد ثبت بالتواتر ما نالهم عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنْ عظيم إذايةِ الخلْقِ بسببِ دعائهم إلى اللهِ تعالى ، حتى إنَّهم تجاسروا على أفضل الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فَآذُوهُ ، وضيقوا عليهِ ، حتى إنهم كسروا رَباعِيَّتَهُ ، وأَدْمَوا منه ذلك الوجْهَ الأبهى الأرفع الكريم ، وحُجِبوا لشقائهم عن مشاهدة تلك المحاسن التي الكشف عن أدناها يَذْهَشُ الفكر ، ويُسْكِرُ النفسَ ؛ بما ترى مِنْ خَرْقِ العادةِ في ذلكَ الخَلْقِ الوسيم ، والخُلُقِ العظيمِ وكيف يفلح قومٌ أدْمَوا وجْهَ نبيّهم الرؤوف عليهم وقدِ استقبلهم بشموس طلعته ، ومحاسن قمرِ وَجْهِهِ ، مُباشراً لهم بتلك الذاتِ الزكيَّةِ المرفّعةِ ؛ ليأخذ بحُجَزِهم عن النار ، حريصاً على ردّهم عنها ولو بالسيف قبل أن يفوتهم الأمرُ بالحلول في دار البوارِ فهذا كلُّه يدلُّ بمُجرَّده على أنَّهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام صادقون في كلَّ ما أَتَوا بهِ عنِ الله تعالى ، وقرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة .
Upon them be prayers and peace: commitment to truthfulness, raising of aspiration from every baseness, and asceticism in the whole world such that its gold and its dust are equal in their eyes, and commitment to utmost humility with the poor and needy, and abandoning status and rank with creation, and seeking it with the True King, and the great compassion with which they were created for creatures, and complete sincerity to the servants of God Most High, and abundance of all fear of Him, and haste to comply with what they conveyed from Him before everyone else, and perseverance until death in calling creation to God Most High, with equality in that between their lowly and their noble, their rich and their poor, their intelligent and their dull, their non-Arab and their eloquent, their free and their slave, their male and their female, their present and their absent, their king and their market-goers. Then broadness of chest to bear the evil of their harm and the severity of their harshness, and compassion for all of them more than their compassion for their own children, nay than for themselves, without any compensation they take from them, nor any worldly benefit that accrues to them from them; rather, they (upon them be prayers and peace) exposed themselves thereby to severe hardships and terrors that befell them from their direction, which none withstands except one who is on solid truth, whom delight in the pleasure of his Master has distracted from considering great anything that brings him to his goal and desire. And it has been established by tawatur (mass transmission) what befell them, upon them be prayers and peace, of great harm from creation due to their calling to God Most High, so much so that they dared against the best of creation and the most honored of them with God, our Prophet and our Master Muhammad (may God bless him and grant him peace), and they harmed him, and constrained him, until they broke his incisor tooth, and made bleed from him that most radiant, most elevated, noble face, and they were veiled by their wretchedness from witnessing those beauties the unveiling of the least of which bewilders the mind and intoxicates the soul, due to what is seen of the breaking of custom in that beautiful form and great character. And how can a people succeed who made bleed the face of their merciful Prophet, while he faced them with the suns of his countenance and the beauties of the moon of his face, directly present to them with that pure, exalted essence, to seize them by their waistbands from the Fire, eager to turn them back from it even by the sword before they enter the abode of perdition? So all of this indicates by its mere self that they (upon them be prayers and peace) are truthful in all that they brought from God Most High, and the qarīna (indicative circumstance) of their state alone precludes the state of lying necessarily.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage is a proof by Sanusi demonstrating that the prophets (upon them peace) are truthful in their message from God, based on their moral character and conduct—a proof independent of miracles. Sanusi proceeds by enumerating the prophet's manifest qualities. First, they are committed to truthfulness in all affairs, they elevate their aspirations above anything base, and they practice such complete asceticism in this world that gold and dust are equal to them. Second, they practice extreme humility with the poor and needy and renounce status and rank among people, seeking only honor with God. Third, they are inherently compassionate toward all creatures, give sincere counsel to God's servants, and possess intense fear of God. Fourth, they hasten to obey what they have conveyed from God, more than anyone else. Fifth, they persist until death in calling people to God, treating all equally regardless of social status, wealth, intelligence, language, freedom, gender, presence, or rank—king and commoner alike. Sixth, they possess such broad-heartedness that they bear the harm and harshness of people with compassion greater than people have for their own children or themselves, without seeking any worldly compensation or benefit. In fact, they expose themselves to severe hardships and terrors from people, which only a person grounded in truth can endure, being so absorbed in seeking God's pleasure that no trial distracts him. Sanusi then notes that it is mass-transmitted (tawatur) how much harm the prophets suffered due to their call, especially the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him)—people dared to harm him, constrained him, broke his tooth, and made his noble face bleed. They were veiled from seeing his extraordinary beauty of form and character, which would overwhelm the mind and intoxicate the soul. Sanusi rhetorically asks: how can a people succeed who caused their merciful Prophet's face to bleed, while he faced them with radiant beauty, personally striving to save them from the Fire even by the sword? The cumulative effect of all these qualities and sacrifices, Sanusi concludes, by their mere existence indicates that the prophets are truthful in everything they conveyed from God. The 'qarīna' (indicative circumstance) of their state alone necessarily precludes lying. This proof relies on the coherence of their moral perfection, their unwavering commitment, and their willingness to suffer for others without worldly gain—all of which are incompatible with falsehood.

الزهد
الشفقة
قرينة حال

Correction: Sanusi shows that the prophets' moral conduct and selfless endurance alone suffice as a proof, independent of miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
Sanusi argues that the prophets' complete asceticism (gold and dust equal) and lack of worldly motive prove their truthfulness. Examine your own heart: is there any worldly gain—status, comfort, or approval—that you would not give up for the sake of truth? What one attachment are you most afraid to surrender, and what would it look like to let it go?
?
The prophets showed more compassion to others than people have for their own children. Think of someone you find difficult to love or forgive. How would you treat them if you had the compassion of a prophet? What is one concrete step you can take today to extend that kind of mercy, even if it costs you something?

The Necessary Truthfulness of the Prophets
Sanusi proves prophetic truthfulness through harm and miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the endurance of harm and miracles establish the truthfulness of prophets as a rational necessity.

Core Idea
The prophets' truthfulness is known necessarily through their state and miracles.

Sanusi presents a powerful argument that the truthfulness of prophets is not merely a matter of hearsay, but is known with certainty (darura) to any divinely guided person. He points to two compelling pieces of evidence: the immense harm the prophets endured while calling to God, and the unmistakable miracles that supported them. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the emotional tone describing the Prophet's suffering.
2
Identify the two proofs
The passage presents two main proofs for truthfulness: the prophets' patience under severe harm, and the miracles (khawariq) they performed. Find these two sections.
The first proof is based on their state (qarina halihim), the second on miraculous acts.
3
Understand the miracle argument
Sanusi argues that miracles cannot be produced by tricks or natural sciences. If they could, others would have done so. Reflect on why this supports truthfulness.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The passage concludes that prophetic truthfulness is known necessarily (darura) to every divinely guided person. Note that this is not just a theological opinion but a rational certainty.
The footnote references Imam al-Haramayn as source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مولاه ، عن أن يستعظم شيئاً يوصله إلى مرادِهِ منه ومناه وقد ثبت بالتواتر ما نالهم عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنْ عظيم إذايةِ الخلْقِ بسببِ دعائهم إلى اللهِ تعالى ، حتى إنَّهم تجاسروا على أفضل الخلْقِ وأكرمهم على الله تعالى نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ فَآذُوهُ ، وضيقوا عليهِ ، حتى إنهم كسروا رَباعِيَّتَهُ ، وأَدْمَوا منه ذلك الوجْهَ الأبهى الأرفع الكريم ، وحُجِبوا لشقائهم عن مشاهدة تلك المحاسن التي الكشف عن أدناها يَذْهَشُ الفكر ، ويُسْكِرُ النفسَ ؛ بما ترى مِنْ خَرْقِ العادةِ في ذلكَ الخَلْقِ الوسيم ، والخُلُقِ العظيمِ وكيف يفلح قومٌ أدْمَوا وجْهَ نبيّهم الرؤوف عليهم وقدِ استقبلهم بشموس طلعته ، ومحاسن قمرِ وَجْهِهِ ، مُباشراً لهم بتلك الذاتِ الزكيَّةِ المرفّعةِ ؛ ليأخذ بحُجَزِهم عن النار ، حريصاً على ردّهم عنها ولو بالسيف قبل أن يفوتهم الأمرُ بالحلول في دار البوارِ ؟! فهذا كلُّه يدلُّ بمُجرَّده على أنَّهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام صادقون في كلَّ ما أَتَوا بهِ عنِ الله تعالى ، وقرينة حالهم وحدها تنافي حالة الكذب ضرورة . كيف وقد أيَّدَهمُ الله تعالى بخوارقَ يُقطَعُ بِأَنَّهُ لا يُتوصَّلُ إليها بحيلة سحرٍ ولا غوص في طب ولا غيره ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وفلْقِ البحر أطواداً ، ونحو ذلكَ ممَّا لا يُتوصَّلُ إليهِ بالحِيَلِ ؛ إذْ لو كانَ يُتوصَّلُ إليه بالحِيَل لاستحال عادةً أن ينفردوا بذلك عن جميع أهل الأرض ؟! هذا ؛ وقد عُلِمَ ضرورةً أنَّهم كانوا في غاية البعدِ عن هذه العلوم وأربابها وأسبابها ، ﴿ وَمَا كُنتَ تَتْلُوا مِن قَبْلِهِ، مِن كِتَبٍ وَلَا تَنْظُمُ بِيَمِينِكَ إِذَا لَّاَرْتابَ الْمُبْطِلُونَ ﴾ [العنكبوت : ٤٨] ، وهذا ممَّا أقرَّ به الموافق والمخالف هذا معَ أنَّ في نفوس الأعداء والحسدة ما يُحرِّكُ الدواعي إلى البحث والتفتيش ، والعادة تحيل أن تكون لهم نسبةٌ إلى شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ إلا ويُعلَمُ ويُقرَّعونَ بهِ ، ويَشتهِرُ أمره حتى لا يخفى على أحدٍ وبالجملة : فصِدْقُ الرُّسُل عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ معلوم على الضرورة لكلِّ مُوفَّقٍ إنَّما أطلتُ بذكرِ هـذا المثال (۱) ، وبذكْرِ ما يطابقهُ مِنْ أحوالِ (1) أصل هذا المثال عند إمام الحرمين في ( الإرشاد ) ( ص ٣٢٥ ) ، و العقيدة النظامية » ( ص ٦٧ ) .
From his Lord, that he should consider great anything that leads him to his desire and wish. And it has been established by recurrent transmission (tawatur) what befell them, peace be upon them, of great harm from creation due to their calling to God Almighty, until they dared against the best of creation and the most honored to God Almighty, our Prophet and Master Muhammad, peace be upon him, and they harmed him, and made things difficult for him, until they broke his front tooth, and caused to bleed that most radiant, most exalted, noble face, and they were veiled by their wretchedness from witnessing those beauties, the disclosure of the least of which bewilders the mind and intoxicates the soul, due to what you see of breaking of custom in that handsome form and great character. And how can a people succeed who caused to bleed the face of their kind prophet, while he faced them with the suns of his countenance and the beauties of the moon of his face, directly confronting them with that pure, elevated essence, to take hold of their waistbands from the Fire, eager to turn them back from it even with the sword before they fall into the abode of perdition?! So all this by itself indicates that they, peace be upon them, are truthful in everything they brought from God Almighty, and the evidence of their state alone necessarily precludes the state of lying. How [could they be liars] when God Almighty supported them with miracles (khawariq) about which it is certain that they cannot be attained by any trick of sorcery, nor by delving into medicine or otherwise, such as reviving the dead, cleaving the sea into mountains, and the like of what cannot be attained by tricks; for if they could be attained by tricks, it would be impossible by custom for them to be unique in that among all the people of the earth?! And it is known necessarily that they were in the utmost distance from these sciences, their masters, and their means. ﴾And you were not reciting before it any book, nor did you inscribe it with your right hand; then the falsifiers would have doubted.﴿ [Al-Ankabut: 48]. And this is something acknowledged by both those who agree and those who disagree. This, while in the souls of enemies and enviers there is what moves the motives to investigation and scrutiny, and custom precludes that they have any connection to any of that unless it would be known and they would be reproached for it, and its affair would become so widespread that it would not be hidden from anyone. In summary: The truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them, is known necessarily to every divinely guided one. I have only gone on at length by mentioning this example (1), and by mentioning what corresponds to it of states. (1) The origin of this example is with Imam al-Haramayn in al-Irshad (p. 325) and al-'Aqida al-Nizamiyya (p. 67).
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the necessary truthfulness of the prophets. The author begins by noting that the prophets endured extreme harm from their people while calling them to God. In particular, the Prophet Muhammad's face was bloodied and his tooth broken by those he sought to save from the Fire. This alone, the author argues, indicates their truthfulness because a liar would not endure such hardship for his mission. Next, the author points to the miracles (khawariq) that God supported them with, such as reviving the dead and parting the sea. These miracles cannot be produced by any trick or natural science; if they could, others would have produced similar feats. Moreover, the prophets were known to be unlettered and far from such knowledge, as the Qur'anic verse confirms. The author adds that enemies and skeptics would have exposed any connection to such knowledge, but no such exposure occurred. Therefore, the truthfulness of the prophets is known necessarily (darura) to anyone divinely guided. The footnote cites Imam al-Haramayn's works as the source of this example.

الخوارق
الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophetic truthfulness is known only through transmitted tradition.
Correction: The passage shows it is known necessarily through rational evidence: their patience and miracles.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face trials or rejection because of your faith, do you remain steadfast like the prophets, or do you complain and give in? The Prophet (peace be upon him) had his tooth broken and his face bloodied, yet he continued calling with mercy. Is your state such that it proves your truthfulness in what you claim to believe?
?
You claim to believe that the Prophet is truthful with absolute certainty—but do you live as if every command he brought is true? If you truly knew by necessity that he is truthful, would you still delay or ignore his teachings? What area of your life today stands in opposition to this necessary truth?
?
The passage says the prophets' state alone is conclusive proof of their truthfulness. If someone judged your faith based solely on your character and endurance under hardship, would they conclude that you truly believe in what you profess? What change must you make so that your state matches your claim?

The Miracle as Divine Attestation: The King's Analogy
Sanusi summarizes the miraculous attestation with an analogy of a king confirming a messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle functions as a divine attestation that produces necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness, illustrated by the king's analogy.

Core Idea
A miracle is like a king breaking custom to confirm his messenger—it produces undeniable knowledge.

Sanusi has explained the logical proof for prophethood. Now he summarizes the conclusive indication of a miracle: it takes the place of an explicit statement from God. To make this vivid, he gives a powerful analogy that shows why miracles produce certainty, not just probability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full translation. Notice how Sanusi first states the principle and then illustrates it with an analogy.
The analogy is designed to make the abstract principle concrete.
2
Grasp the principle
Identify the claim: a miracle takes the rank of explicit attestation (تصديق صريح) from God. Understand the reason: God's custom is to create necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) of truthfulness after a miracle.
This is the core of the proof—miracles produce certainty, not inference.
3
Analyze the analogy
See how the king's action (breaking custom) mirrors God's action (breaking natural laws). The people's reaction (certainty) mirrors the necessary knowledge gained from a miracle.
The analogy shows why doubt is removed—the king's act is a direct confirmation.
4
Reflect on the outcome
Ask yourself: why does a miracle produce 'necessary knowledge'? Because it is as if God is speaking directly. This makes prophethood rationally certain.
This connects to the broader argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل ما أشار إليه في بيان وجه دلالة المعجزة (٢) : أنَّها عندَ التحقيق تتنزَّلُ منزلة صريح التصديقِ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى لَمَنْ ظهرَتْ على يده ; لما جَرَتْ بهِ العادةُ مِنْ أَنَّ اللهَ تعالى يخلُقُ عَقيبَها العلم الضروري بالصِّدْقِ ، كما إذا قام رجلٌ في مجلس ملك بحضورِ جماعة ، وادَّعى أنَّهُ رسولُ هذا الملكِ إليهم ، فطالبوه بالحُجَّةِ ، فقال : هي أن يخرقَ الملك عادته ويقوم عن سريرِهِ ويقعد ثلاثَ مَرَّاتٍ مثلاً ، ففعل ، فإنَّهُ يكون تصديقاً ومفيداً للعلم الضروري بصِدْقِهِ مِنْ غير ارتياب .
And the summary of what he indicated in clarifying the aspect of the miracle's indication (2) is that it, upon investigation, takes the rank of explicit attestation from God Almighty for the one on whose hand it appears; because of the established custom that God Almighty creates after it necessary knowledge of truthfulness. Just as when a man stands in a king's assembly in the presence of a group, and claims that he is the messenger of this king to them, and they demand proof from him, and he says: 'It is that the king break his custom, and rise from his throne, and sit down three times, for example,' and he does it, then it is an attestation and productive of necessary knowledge of his truthfulness without any doubt.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is a summary of the principle (حاصل) concerning how a miracle functions as a proof of prophethood. The author states that when examined truly, a miracle takes the place of an explicit verbal attestation (تصديق صريح) from God for the person who performs it. The reason is that God's normal way (جري العادة) is that He creates, immediately upon the occurrence of a miracle, necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) of the truthfulness of the claimant. To illustrate, the author provides a powerful analogy: imagine a man stands before a king in an assembly, claiming to be the king's messenger. The people demand proof. The man says his proof is that the king will break his usual behavior—rising from his throne and sitting down three times. If the king then does exactly that, it constitutes a clear attestation, producing necessary knowledge of the man's truthfulness without any doubt (من غير ارتياب). In the same way, when a prophet performs a miracle, it is as if God Himself is breaking His normal course of nature to confirm the prophet's message, and this yields certain, undeniable knowledge.

Key Terms
دَلالة المعجزة
تصديق صريح
علم ضروري
جري العادة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles prove prophethood through inference or logical deduction rather than immediate certainty.
Correction: The passage shows that a miracle produces necessary knowledge (علم ضروري) directly, like witnessing the king's action, not through inference.

Checkpoint
According to the author, how does a miracle function as a proof of truthfulness?
A) It creates a logical syllogism
B) It takes the place of explicit attestation from God and produces necessary knowledge of truthfulness
C) It is a sign that can be understood only by scholars
D) It proves the prophet's superior knowledge

Key Takeaway
A miracle is equivalent to God's explicit confirmation, producing necessary knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness without any doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
This lesson claims that after a miracle, knowledge is immediate and undeniable. But have you ever felt that your faith wavers despite knowing the miracles? Perhaps you have not fully internalized that this knowledge is from God Himself. Will you ask God tonight to plant that necessary knowledge firmly in your heart?

The Example of the King's Messenger: Illustration, Not Analogy
Sanusi explains that the king example is for clarification, not analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the king's messenger example is used only for clarification and not as an analogical argument in proving prophethood.

Core Idea
The king's messenger example clarifies miracles; it does not prove them by analogy.

Sanusi presents a vivid example of a king breaking his custom to attest a messenger. But this example is not the actual proof; it is a teaching tool. In this lesson, you will see how an objection based on the weakness of analogy is answered, and why the example remains valuable for beginners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation once to get the overall flow of the argument. Notice that the passage includes a summary, an example, an objection, and an answer.
Pay attention to the objection introduced by 'واعتُرِضَ' and the answer with 'والجواب'.
2
Identify the objection
The objector claims the king example is an analogy from the visible to the unseen, which is only valid for probability, not certainty in foundational matters. Find the exact wording for this objection.
The objection includes the phrase 'قياس الغائب على الشاهد'.
3
Study Sanusi's answer
Sanusi responds that the example was never meant for analogy (قياس) but for clarification (توضيح) and confirmation (تقرير). Understand why this distinction is crucial.
Look for the phrase 'لم يُذكَر للقياس والاستدلال'.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical purpose
Consider why examples from the visible world are useful despite not being formal proofs. How does familiarity help a beginner grasp the concept of a miracle's indication?
Sanusi mentions that the intellect's darkness is dispelled when the example clarifies the analogous unseen case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل ما أشار إليه في بيان وجه دلالة المعجزة: أنَّها عند التحقيق تتنزَّل منزلة صريح التصديق من الله تعالى لمن ظهرت على يده؛ لما جرت به العادة من أن الله تعالى يخلق عقيبها العلم الضروري بالصدق، كما إذا قام رجل في مجلس ملك بحضور جماعة، وادعى أنَّه رسول هذا الملك إليهم، فطالبوه بالحجة، فقال: هي أن يخرق الملك عادته ويقوم عن سريره ويقعد ثلاث مرات مثلاً، ففعل، فإنَّه يكون تصديقاً ومفيداً للعلم الضروري بصدقه من غير ارتياب. واعتُرِضَ: بأنَّ هذا تمثيل، وقياس للغائب على الشاهد وهو على تقدير ظهور الجامع إنَّما يُعتبر في العمليَّات لإفادة الظن، وقد اعتبر تموه بلا جامع لإفادة اليقين في العلميَّات التي هي أساس ثبوت الشرائع! على أنَّ حصول العلم فيما ذكرتم من المثال إنَّما شُوهِدَ من قرائن الأحوال، وأين هو في حق الغائبين المحجوبين كما في مسألتنا؟! والجواب: أنَّ هذا المثال لم يُذكَر للقياس والاستدلال، وإنَّما ذكر للتوضيح والتقرير؛ لأنَّ الف الإنسان للشاهد وأنسه به أكثر، فإذا قرع سمعه وأحضره بذهنه، وقبل عقله الدلالة فيه، وفهم وجهها ضرورة.. انجلى عن العقل حينئذ ظلمة استصعابه فهم النظير لعدم إلفه به؛ وهو وجه دلالة المعجزة، وصار عنده واضحاً كالشمس ضرورياً لا يُقلَّد فيه أحداً، ولا يقول عقله عند ذلك: سمعت الناس يقولون شيئاً فقلته. فذكر هذا المثال إنَّما هو من باب العبارات التي يُقرَّب بها على المبتدئ الفهم، ويُوضَح له به المعنى من غير عسر، وإلا فمُدرَك دلالة المعجزة ضروري لمن حقَّق أركانها بمعرفة توحيد الله تعالى.
The summary of what he referred to in explaining the mode of indication of the miracle is that it, upon investigation, occupies the position of explicit attestation from Allah Almighty for the one on whose hand it appears, because of the established custom that Allah Almighty creates after it necessary knowledge of truthfulness, just as if a man stands up in a king’s assembly in the presence of a group and claims that he is the messenger of this king to them, and they demand a proof from him, and he says: 'It is that the king breaks his custom, rises from his throne, and sits down three times, for example,' and he does so, then that becomes an attestation and productive of necessary knowledge of his truthfulness without any doubt. And it was objected: that this is an analogy, and a comparison of the absent to the present, and even if a common feature appears, it is only considered in practical matters to produce probability, and they have presumptuously considered it without a common feature to produce certainty in theoretical matters which are the foundation of the establishment of the laws! Moreover, the occurrence of knowledge in the example you mentioned is only observed from circumstantial evidence, and where is it with respect to the absent and veiled ones as in our issue?! The answer: that this example was not mentioned for analogy and inference, but rather was mentioned for clarification and confirmation, because man’s familiarity with the present and his attachment to it is greater, so when it strikes his hearing and he brings it to his mind, and his intellect accepts the indication in it and understands its mode necessarily, then the darkness of his difficulty in understanding the analogous one due to his lack of familiarity with it – which is the mode of indication of the miracle – is dispelled from his intellect, and it becomes clear as the sun, necessary, not imitating anyone, and his intellect does not say at that: 'I heard people saying something, so I said it.' So the mention of this example is only from the category of expressions by which understanding is facilitated for the beginner and the meaning is clarified to him without difficulty. Otherwise, the perceptual apprehension of the indication of the miracle is necessary for one who has verified its pillars by knowing the oneness of Allah Almighty.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section within the broader discussion of proving prophethood through miracles. Sanusi begins by summarizing the standard account: a miracle, by divine custom, produces necessary knowledge of the truthfulness of the prophet, just as a king’s breaking of his own custom in the presence of witnesses produces certain knowledge that the messenger is truthful. Then an objection is raised: this example is merely an analogy from the visible to the unseen, and even if a common factor were present, analogies only yield probability in practical matters, not certainty in theoretical matters which are the foundation of religious laws. Moreover, the knowledge in the example comes from immediate sensory observation, which is absent for later generations who did not witness the miracle. The answer is crucial: the example was never intended as an analogical argument. It is only a pedagogical tool to clarify the concept. People are naturally more familiar with visible scenarios; once they understand the logical force of the king’s action in that familiar case, their minds can transfer that understanding to the unseen case—not by logical analogy, but by grasping the identical underlying principle: that a miraculous action breaking custom is a divine attestation. Thus the example removes the mental barrier of unfamiliarity and makes the necessary knowledge intuitive. Sanusi emphasizes that for those who truly understand the foundations (tawhid and the conditions of miracles), the indication of a miracle is itself necessary knowledge, not dependent on such examples. The passage guards against the misunderstanding that the kalam proof for prophethood relies on a weak analogy from the visible world.

Key Terms
المعجزة
العلم الضروري
وجه الدلالة
تمثيل
قياس الغائب على الشاهد
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The king example is used as an analogical proof for prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi explicitly states it is only for clarification, not for analogy (قياس).

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's response to the objection, what is the purpose of the king example?
A) To provide an analogical argument from the visible world to the unseen.
B) To serve as a historical proof for the truthfulness of a specific prophet.
C) To clarify the mode of indication of miracles for beginners who are more familiar with visible examples.
D) To demonstrate that miracles produce only probable knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi's king example is a pedagogical tool to clarify the mode of indication of miracles, not an analogical proof, and the real evidence for prophethood is the miracle itself when its conditions are met.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Objection Against the Miracle Example and Its Answer
Sanusi refutes objection that miracle example is invalid qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the king-and-reporter example is not a logical proof but a pedagogical tool, and how it removes confusion about the evidential force of miracles.

Core Idea
Miracle evidence needs no analogy; examples only clarify for beginners.

Sanusi introduces a hypothetical objection that his king-and-reporter example is an invalid analogy. He then provides a clear response, distinguishing between proof and illustration. This lesson examines that exchange and clarifies the role of examples in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once. Notice the objection and the beginning of the answer. Then read the translation.
The passage is a single coherent argument.
2
Identify the objection
The objector claims the example is an invalid qiyas from unseen to witnessed, only producing conjecture, not certainty. Also, the example relies on circumstantial evidence not available for the unseen.
3
Analyze the answer
The author responds that the example is for clarification, not proof. Because humans are familiar with the witnessed, the example removes mental difficulty and makes the miracle's indication intuitive.
Note the emphasis on ضروري (necessary knowledge) for one who knows tawhid.
4
Reflect on the pedagogical purpose
Understand that the example is a teaching tool for beginners, not a logical foundation. For the advanced, miracle evidence is self-evident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذكر مثال الملك والمبلغ عنه للتوضيح لا للاستدلال. واعتُرِضَ بأنَّ هذا تمثيل، وقياس للغائب على الشاهد، وهو على تقدير ظهور الجامع إنما يعتبر في العمليات لإفادة الظن، وقد اعتبر تموه بلا جامع لإفادة اليقين في العلميات التي هي أساس ثبوت الشرائع. على أن حصول العلم فيما ذكرتم من المثال إنما شوهد من قرائن الأحوال، وأين هو في حق الغائبين المحجوبين كما في مسألتنا؟ والجواب: أنَّ هذا المثال لم يذكر للقياس والاستدلال، وإنما ذكر للتوضيح والتقرير؛ لأنَّ ألف الإنسان للشاهد وأنسه به أكثر، فإذا قرع سمعه وأحضره بذهنه، وقبل عقله الدلالة فيه، وفهم وجهها ضرورة.. انجلى عن العقل حينئذ ظلمة استصعابه فهم النظير لعدم إلفه به؛ وهو وجه دلالة المعجزة، وصار عنده واضحاً كالشمس ضرورياً لا يقلد فيه أحداً، ولا يقول عقله عند ذلك: سمعت الناس يقولون شيئاً فقلته. فذكر هذا المثال إنما هو من باب العبارات التي يقرب بها على المبتدئ الفهم، ويوضح له به المعنى من غير عسر، وإلا فمدرك دلالة المعجزة ضروري لمن حقق أركانها بمعرفة توحيد الله تعالى ومعرفة صفاته، ولا يفتقر في دلالتها إلى مثال يضرب في الشاهد أصلاً.
He mentioned the example of the king and the reporter [about him] for clarification, not for proof. An objection was raised: this is an analogy, a qiyas from the unseen to the witnessed. Even if there is a commonality, it is only considered in practical matters to produce conjecture, and it has been used without a commonality to produce certainty in theoretical matters, which are the foundation of establishing the laws. Moreover, the obtaining of knowledge in the example you mentioned was observed from circumstantial evidence; where is that in the case of the absent hidden ones as in our issue? The answer: this example was not mentioned for qiyas and proof, but only for clarification and explanation, because man's familiarity with the witnessed and his intimacy with it is greater. So when it sounds in his ear and he brings it to mind, and his mind accepts the indication and understands its aspect necessarily, then the darkness of his difficulty in understanding the similar [unseen] due to lack of familiarity with it is removed from the mind; and that is the aspect of the indication of the miracle. And it becomes clear to him like the sun, necessary, not imitating anyone, and his mind does not say: I heard people say something so I said it. So this example is only from the category of expressions by which understanding is made near to the beginner, and the meaning is clarified to him without difficulty. Otherwise, the locus of perception of the indication of the miracle is necessary for one who has realized its pillars by knowing tawhid of Allah and knowing His attributes, and it does not need an example made in the witnessed at all.
Source pages p. 450

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the use of a king-and-reporter example to illustrate miracle evidence, followed by the author's answer. The objector claims the example constitutes an invalid qiyas (analogy) from the unseen to the witnessed, which only yields conjecture in practical matters, not certainty in theoretical matters like establishing divine law. Furthermore, the knowledge gained from the example comes from observed circumstantial evidence, unavailable for the unseen prophets. The answer refutes this by clarifying that the example is not used as a proof (استدلال) but merely for clarification (توضيح) and explanation (تقرير). Because humans are more familiar with the witnessed, bringing such an example to mind helps remove mental difficulty in understanding a similar unseen reality—here, the evidential force of miracles. After understanding the example, the mind perceives the miracle's indication as clear as the sun, necessarily, without reliance on authority. Thus, the example is a pedagogical tool for beginners. In reality, for one who has properly realized the pillars of a miracle—knowledge of Allah's tawhid and attributes—the evidential force of miracles is intuitive (ضروري) and needs no witnessed example.

Key Terms
قياس الغائب على الشاهد
دلالة المعجزة
ضروري
ظن
يقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the author is using analogy as proof.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the example is only for illustration, not for proof. The actual evidence for miracles is intuitive for those who know tawhid.

Checkpoint

A) To serve as a logical proof for prophethood through qiyas.
B) To clarify and make understanding easier for beginners.
C) To imitate the method of the philosophers.
D) To cast doubt on the necessity of miracles.

Key Takeaway
The king-and-reporter example is a pedagogical tool, not a proof; miracle evidence is intuitive for one who knows tawhid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Ignorance of Miracle Pillars Causes Denial
Sanusi explains two errors causing denial of miracle evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that denial of miraculous proof for prophethood is rooted in ignorance of the foundations of miracles, specifically regarding Allah's free agency and the supernatural nature of miracles.

Core Idea
Denial of miracles is not malice but ignorance of their pillars.

Why do some people reject the clear evidence of miracles? Sanusi diagnoses the root cause: ignorance of what makes a miracle a miracle. This lesson unpacks two specific errors that lead to denial, showing that the issue is theological blindness, not intellectual deficiency. Read on to see how the philosophers and naturalists go wrong.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi begins with a strong claim about the cause of denial.
The passage is cut off at the end; focus on the complete argument about the two errors.
2
Identify the two errors
The passage lists two specific ways people are ignorant of the pillars of miracles. Find each one and note how they relate to tawhid.
The first error involves philosophers, the second involves those who think miracles are tricks.
3
Reflect on the cure
The passage hints that guidance comes from proper tawhid. Ask yourself: how does knowing Allah as the Free Agent solve these errors?
This connects to the broader topic of prophethood and divine attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا قالوا : ما أُتِيَ أحدٌ مِنْ منكري النبوَّاتِ في جَحْدِ دَلالةِ المعجزاتِ إِلا مِنْ وجه الجهل بأركانها؛ فقد يجهلُ أنَّ الخارق للعادةِ فعلُ اللهِ تعالى، ولا يعتقد الصانع المختار، بل يعتقد صدور العالم عن علةٍ تُوجِبُ بالذَّاتِ بتوسطِ عقول ونفوس وحركاتِ أفلاك وطبائع كما تدعيه الفلاسفة والطبائعيونَ؛ لجهلهم بمعرفة الله تعالى ووحدانيته، وقد يعتقدُ أنَّهُ ليسَ خارقاً للعادة، وأنَّهُ ممَّا يجوزُ التوصُّلُ إليه بالحِيلِ والغوص في العلوم. فأَمَّا مَنْ هُدِيَ لمسلكِ الحقِّ، وعرف بما تقرَّرَ عندَهُ مِنَ التوحيدِ أَنَّ...
And because of this they said: None of the deniers of prophethood ever came to deny the indication of miracles except from the aspect of ignorance of its pillars. For he may be ignorant that the supernatural act is the act of Allah, and he does not believe in the Free Agent, but rather believes in the emanation of the world from a cause that necessitates by essence through the mediation of intellects, souls, movements of spheres, and natures, as the philosophers and naturalists claim, due to their ignorance of knowledge of Allah and His oneness. And he may believe that it is not supernatural, and that it is from what can be attained by tricks and deep study of sciences. As for one who has been guided to the path of truth, and knows through what has been established with him of tawhid that...
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage explains the root cause of denying miracles: ignorance of their pillars (أركان). The author states that every denier of prophethood fails to grasp the evidential force of miracles due to such ignorance. Two specific errors are mentioned: (1) Some, like philosophers and naturalists, do not recognize Allah as the Free Agent (الصانع المختار); they believe the world emanates necessarily from a cause, through intermediaries like intellects, souls, celestial spheres, and natures. They reject that Allah directly produces supernatural events. (2) Others may think the miracle is not actually supernatural but achievable through tricks or deep scientific knowledge. Thus, both errors stem from ignorance of tawhid and Allah's attributes. The passage concludes by contrasting those who are guided to the true path, having properly established tawhid in their minds—implying they will accept the evidence of miracles. The sentence is cut off here, but the intended completion is that such a person will undoubtedly affirm prophethood.

أركان المعجزة
الصانع المختار
الخارق للعادة
توحيد
علة موجبة بالذات

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People deny miracles because they are stubborn or evil.
Correction: The passage shows denial is due to ignorance of theological principles, specifically the pillars of miracles and tawhid.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason people deny the indication of miracles?
A) They are intellectually incapable of understanding.
B) They are stubborn and rebellious.
C) Ignorance of the pillars of miracles.
D) They have not seen a miracle themselves.

Key Takeaway
Denial of miracles is rooted in ignorance of two key truths: Allah's free agency and the supernatural nature of miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about miracles, do you ever find yourself subconsciously looking for natural explanations? Which of the two errors Sanusi describes is more tempting for you, and what does that reveal about your own knowledge of tawhid?
?
Sanusi says that denial of miracles comes from ignorance—not just lack of information, but a failure to know Allah as He truly is. In your daily life, where might your ignorance be blocking you from recognizing Allah's signs? What will you do today to remove that ignorance?
?
Philosophers and naturalists thought they were rational, but Sanusi diagnoses their real problem as ignorance of Allah's oneness. Are there areas of your faith where you trust your own reasoning more than the truths of tawhid? What would it mean for you to repent from that intellectual pride?

Necessary Knowledge from Miracles
Sanusi on necessary knowledge from miracles and rebuttal of circumstantial evidence objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles produce necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness and how Sanusi refutes the objection that such knowledge depends on circumstantial evidence.

Core Idea
Miracles yield necessary, not subjective, knowledge of prophethood.

Sanusi explains that a miracle, known to be from Allah and impossible by trickery, gives the observer immediate necessary knowledge of the prophet's truth. He then addresses a common objection—that this knowledge actually comes from surrounding circumstances—by showing that the same necessary knowledge arises even for absent people through tawatur and in a hypothetical scenario where circumstances are controlled. This passage firmly grounds prophetic verification in clear divine action rather than subjective context.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditions for necessary knowledge
Read how Sanusi lists the conditions: the act is from Allah, the claimant knows the challenge, the act is extraordinary and not from trickery.
This sets the basis for the argument.
2
See how knowledge is attained
Once these conditions are met, necessary knowledge of truthfulness follows directly without needing examples.
This is the core claim.
3
Examine the objection
Note the objection that necessary knowledge arises from circumstantial evidence.
Understand the objection.
4
Follow the refutation
Sanusi uses two cases—absent people via tawatur and a king behind veils—to show that knowledge is still necessary independent of circumstances.
This proves the objection wrong.
5
Connect to the broader proof of prophethood
Realize that miracles are objective indicators, not subjective.
This lesson strengthens the argument for prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي وقع به التحدي فعل الله تعالى، وهو عالم بدعوى التحدي إما بمشاهدته أو بالنقل المتواتر، وعرف أنه لا يتوصل إليه بالحيل، إذ أهل الحيل وما يتوصلون بحيلهم أو علومهم إليه معروف لا يخفى إلا على غبي، ثم عرف أن ذلك الفعل الخارق للعادة فعل الله تعالى على وفق دعوى النبي إجابةً له.. لم يسترب في حصول العلم الضروري بصدقه، ولا يحتاج في ذلك إلى مثال ولا غيره. وأما دعوى المعترض: أن ذلك العلم الضروري في المثال إنما ثبت باعتبار قرائن الأحوال.. فليس بصحيح؛ لحصول مثل ذلك العلم الضروري للغائبين عن هذا المجلس عند تواتر القصة إليهم وللحاضرين فيما إذا فرضنا الملك في بيت، وبيننا وبينه حجب منعتنا من رؤيته، وجعل مدعي الرسالة حجته أن يحرك الملك تلك الحجب من ساعته، ففعل، وقد عرفوا أن الملك قد سمع دعواه الرسالة عنه وسمع تحديه بتحريك الملك لتلك الحجب، وعرفوا أن تلك الحجب لم يحركها إلا الملك؛ لأنه لا يقدر على تحريكها أحد سواه. وقد أشرنا نحن في أصل العقيدة إلى ما يفهم منه هذا الجواب في تقرير المثال.
The act by which the challenge occurred is an act of Allah, may He be exalted, and he (the claimant) knows of the claim of the challenge either by witnessing it or by transmitted tawatur, and he knows that it cannot be attained by tricks; for the people of tricks and what they attain by their tricks or sciences are known and not hidden except from a fool. Then he knows that that extraordinary act is an act of Allah, may He be exalted, in accordance with the claim of the prophet as a response to him... he does not doubt in obtaining necessary knowledge of his truthfulness, and he does not need for that an example or anything else. As for the claim of the objector that that necessary knowledge in the example is only established by consideration of circumstances... it is not correct; because such necessary knowledge occurs for those absent from this gathering when the story is transmitted to them via tawatur, and for those present in the case where we suppose a king in a house, and between us and him there are veils that prevent us from seeing him, and the claimant of prophethood makes his proof that the king should move those veils from his hour, and he does so, and they know that the king heard his claim of prophethood and heard his challenge by the king moving those veils, and they know that those veils were moved only by the king because no one else can move them. And we have indicated in the original [work] on creed what is understood from this answer in establishing the example.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage defines how a miracle produces necessary knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness and rebuts a specific objection. It begins by stating the conditions: the act of challenge is known to be from Allah, the claimant knows it, and it is understood that no trickery can produce it. Then, given that the act is extraordinary and matches the claim, the observer attains necessary knowledge of the prophet's sincerity without needing further examples. The objector argues that such knowledge arises only from circumstantial evidence (قرائن الأحوال). Sanusi refutes this by noting that identical necessary knowledge occurs for those not present but receiving the story via tawatur, and for those present in a scenario with a king behind veils where the prophet asks the king to move the veils. In both cases, the knowledge is necessary and arises from clear evidence of divine intervention, not subjective circumstances. He also references his original creedal work for further illustration.

Key Terms
علم ضروري
تحدي
معجزة
قرائن الأحوال
تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The necessary knowledge of a prophet's truth from a miracle is based on the surrounding circumstances and not on the miracle itself.
Correction: Sanusi shows that even those absent (via tawatur) and in controlled scenarios (king behind veils) attain necessary knowledge, proving it is independent of circumstances.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what is the basis for the necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness from a miracle?
A) The subjective circumstances surrounding the event.
B) The clear knowledge that the act is from Allah and matches the challenge, without reliance on circumstances.
C) The trickery of the prophet in performing the act.
D) The opinion of the majority of people.

Key Takeaway
Miracles provide necessary, objective knowledge of a prophet's truth, independent of subjective circumstances.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about a miracle attributed to the Prophet (ﷺ), do you internally feel certainty, or do you find yourself rationalizing it away? What does your response say about your trust in the necessary knowledge that this lesson describes?
?
If your conviction in the prophethood were based only on subjective circumstances, what would happen when those circumstances change? Is your faith grounded in the miracle itself or in your own comfort?
?
The objector in this passage denied necessary knowledge from miracles. Have you ever, in your heart, doubted the clear signs of Allah because you wanted more 'evidence'? What would it take for you to accept a miracle as sufficient proof?

Refutation of the First Atheist Objection: The Miracle Might Not Be from God
Sanusi presents the first atheist objection and its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first atheist objection against miracles and how Sanusi refutes it by affirming that only Allah has true causal power.

Core Idea
Miracles are from Allah alone — no creature or nature can produce them.

The atheists propose that miracles might come from the prophet's own abilities, natural properties, or other beings. Sanusi counters by invoking the foundational kalam principle that Allah is the sole effecter in existence. This lesson clarifies that objection and its decisive answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, focusing on the various possibilities the atheists suggest for the miracle's source.
Notice that they propose natural, angelic, or celestial causes, not just outright denial.
2
Identify the refutation's main argument
Sanusi responds with a previously established proof: no effecter but Allah without intermediary. Understand why this negates all proposed alternatives.
This is a core kalam principle: causality belongs to Allah alone.
3
Reflect on the special evidence from major miracles
Sanusi lists clear examples (reviving dead, staff transformation, moon splitting) that are indisputably divine. Consider why these leave no room for doubt.
He also adds a secondary argument: even if the act were from another, Allah's non-prevention suffices to prove the prophet's truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ رد الاعتراضات والشبه في دلالة المعجزات ]
وقد اعترضت الملحدة - أهلكهم الله تعالى - على دلالة المعجزة باحتمالات لا يخفى على اللبيب جوابها وقد سبق الجواب صريحاً عن بعضها، وهي أنواع (1):
الأول: ألا يكون ذلك الأمر من الله تعالى: بل يستند إلى المدعي لخاصية في نفسه أو مزاج في بدنه، أو لاطلاع منه على خواص في بعض الأجسام يتخذها ذريعة إلى ذلك، أو يستند إلى بعض الملائكة أو الجن، أو اتصالات كوكبية، أو أوضاع فلكية لا يطلع عليها غيره، إلى غير ذلك من الأسباب جميع الكائنات.
وجوابه: أنه قد سبق بالبرهان أن لا مؤثر في إلا الله تعالى بلا واسطة (2)، فلا تأثير لطبيعة ولا خاصية، سيما في مثال إحياء الموتى، وانقلاب العصا، وانشقاق القمر، وسلام الحجر والمدر؛ فإن مثل هذه الأشياء لا شبهة فيها للعاقل أنها من الله تعالى بلا واسطة، ولا يقدر عليها كل ما سواه ألبتة، كما أن ذلك حكم جميع الكائنات عند أهل الحق الموحدين على الحقيقة (3)
على أن مجرد التمكن من فعل تلك الأشياء على تقدير أن تكون تلك الأمور من فعل غيره جل وعلا، وترك الدفع من الحكيم القادر المختار.. كاف في إفادة المطلوب، وإن كنا نقطع بأن هذا التقدير مستحيل.
[Refutation of objections and doubts concerning the evidence of miracles]
And the atheists — may Allah destroy them — have objected to the evidence of the miracle with possibilities whose answer is not hidden from the intelligent, and the answer has already preceded explicitly for some of them. They are of types (1):
The first: That the matter may not be from Allah, may He be exalted, but rather it is attributed to the claimant for a property in himself or a temperament in his body, or his knowledge of properties in some bodies which he uses as a means to that, or it is attributed to some angels or jinn, or planetary conjunctions, or celestial configurations not known to others, and other causes of all things.
And its answer: It has already preceded by proof that there is no effecter in existence except Allah, may He be exalted, without intermediary (2), so there is no effect for nature or property, especially in the example of reviving the dead, the transformation of the staff, the splitting of the moon, and the greeting of the stone and clod; for such things are not doubtful for the intelligent that they are from Allah, may He be exalted, without intermediary, and everything other than Him cannot do them at all, just as that is the judgment of all things according to the people of truth, the true monotheists (3).
Moreover, the mere enabling of doing those things on the assumption that those matters are from the action of other than Him, Glorified and Exalted, and the leaving of prevention from the Wise, Omnipotent, Free Choser... is sufficient to achieve the desired result, even though we are certain that this assumption is impossible.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage presents the first objection of the atheists (الملحدة) against the evidence of miracles and its answer. The section begins with a heading indicating the refutation of objections and doubts. The atheists raise possibilities that the phenomenal act might not be from Allah but from the prophet's own inner property, temperament, knowledge of natural properties, angels/jinn, celestial influences, etc. Sanusi answers with a previously established proof that there is no effecter (لا مؤثر) except Allah without intermediary, so nature and properties have no independent effect. This is especially clear in major miracles like reviving the dead, transforming a staff, splitting the moon, and the greeting of inanimate objects — these are indisputably from Allah alone. He adds that even if we were to assume such acts could come from other than Allah, the fact that Allah enables them and does not prevent them from the Wise, Omnipotent, Free Choser is sufficient to prove the prophet's truthfulness, though we know this assumption is impossible.

Key Terms
ملحدة
معجزة
مؤثر
خاصية
واسطة
أهل الحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles might be due to natural causes, the prophet's own abilities, or other beings like angels or jinn.
Correction: Sanusi shows that only Allah is the true effecter; no creature or natural property can produce a miracle, especially major ones like reviving the dead or splitting the moon.

Checkpoint
What is the first objection of the atheists regarding miracles?
A) That the miracle is merely a coincidence.
B) That the miracle might not be from Allah but from the prophet's own ability or other causes.
C) That the miracle is a lie invented by followers.
D) That the miracle has no meaning.

Key Takeaway
Sanusi establishes that miracles are direct acts of Allah, not attributable to any creature or natural property.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a blessing you received recently. Did you genuinely attribute it to Allah's direct act, or did you subconsciously credit your own effort, a natural cause, or another person? How would your gratitude change if you truly believed 'لا مؤثر في إلا الله'? What one step can you take today to make the recognition of Allah's sole effect more real in your heart?
?
Sanusi says that even if other causes were hypothetically possible, Allah's permission would suffice to prove the prophet's truthfulness. Do you live with the certainty that nothing happens without Allah's will? When was the last time you felt fear of a created thing—like illness, poverty, or another person's opinion—and how does this lesson challenge that fear? Will you consciously remind yourself of this truth the next time you feel afraid?
?
If you were asked to testify that a miracle is from Allah, would you be as certain as Sanusi expects any 'rational person' to be? What doubts might still linger in your mind about God's absolute power over all events? What specific situation in your life makes it hard to see only Allah's hand at work, and how can you actively combat that misperception starting now?

The Second Objection: Miracles as Custom Initiation or Rare Recurrence
Sanusi presents and refutes the second objection to miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection against miracles and Sanusi's decisive refutation based on certain knowledge of supernatural events.

Core Idea
Miracles are not rare natural events; they are known with certainty to be supernatural.

Skeptics sometimes suggest that miracles are not truly supernatural but simply the beginning of a new natural custom or a very rare recurrence of an old one. Sanusi addresses this objection head-on, showing that the miracles of the prophets are so extraordinary that no rational person could mistake them for ordinary phenomena. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, paying attention to the objector's claim: that a miracle might be just a new custom or a rare recurrence.
Note the example of fixed stars returning to a point after long ages.
2
Identify Sanusi's response
Sanusi's answer is direct: we are talking about events known with certainty to be supernatural. Find that phrase in the passage.
3
Examine the examples
List the examples Sanusi gives: bringing dead to life, splitting the sea, splitting the moon, water from fingers. Notice how these are clearly beyond natural custom.
These are from the miracles of the prophets.
4
Understand the refutation's force
Sanusi argues that no rational person doubts that these are supernatural. Therefore, the objection fails because it does not apply to the miracles under discussion.
This shows the objection is irrelevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : يحتمل ألا يكون ذلك الأمر خارقاً للعادة : بل ابتداء عادةٍ أرادَ الله تعالى إجراءَها ، أو تكريرُ عادةٍ لا تكون إلا في دهورٍ متطاولة ، كعود الثوابتِ إلى نقطةٍ مُعيَّنةٍ .
وجوابه : أنَّ كلامَنا فيما حصلَ الجزمُ بأَنَّهُ خارق للعادةِ ليسَ بابتداء عادة ، ولا بإعادةٍ مُتكرّرةٍ ؛ كإحياء الموتى ، وانفلاق البحر أطواداً ، وانشقاق القمرِ ، ونبع الماءِ مِنْ بين الأصابع أمثال العيون ، ونحوِ ذلك ، وكلُّ معجزاتِ الرُّسُلِ لا يتمارى عاقل ولا يرتابُ أنَّها ليسَتْ بشيء مما ذكرَهُ المعترض
The second: It is possible that that matter is not supernatural: rather it is an initiation of a custom that Allah intended to run, or a repetition of a custom that does not occur except in longstanding ages, like the return of fixed stars to a specific point. And its answer: That our speech is concerning what has been known with certainty that it is supernatural, not an initiation of a custom, nor a repeated recurrence; like bringing the dead to life, and the splitting of the sea into mountains, and the splitting of the moon, and the gushing of water from between fingers like springs, and the like of that; and all the miracles of the messengers (upon them peace and blessings) no rational person doubts or hesitates that they are not anything of what the objector mentioned.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the second objection concerning the possibility that a miracle might not be supernatural but rather the initiation of a new custom or a rare recurrence of an old custom. The objector suggests that such events could be mere phenomena that occur at long intervals, like the return of fixed stars to a specific point. Sanusi's answer is straightforward: miracles are known with certainty to be supernatural; they are not customs or rare recurrences. He gives examples like bringing the dead to life, splitting the sea, splitting the moon, and water gushing from fingers. No rational person doubts that these are beyond the ordinary. Thus, the objection fails because the discussion concerns only those events that are definitively supernatural.

Key Terms
خارق للعادة
ابتداء عادة
تكرير عادة
معجزات الرسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think miracles could be explainable as rare natural events that just happen seldom.
Correction: Sanusi argues that prophetic miracles are known with certainty to be supernatural; they are not customs or rare recurrences, as shown by their extraordinary nature.

Checkpoint

A) Miracles could be magic
B) Miracles could be initiation or repetition of a custom
C) Miracles could be the work of jinn
D) Miracles could be coincidences

Key Takeaway
Miracles are known with certainty to be supernatural, and the objection that they might be customs or rare recurrences does not apply to them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The objector says a miracle might just be a rare natural recurrence. Have you ever rationalized a miracle from the Qur'an or Sunnah to make it 'more believable' to yourself or others? How does that insult Allah's power and the purpose of miracles as signs of certainty?
?
Sanusi says 'no rational person doubts' these miracles. But do you? What areas of your faith do you secretly harbor doubts about, and what would it cost you to seek certainty like the companions did?

Third Objection: The Possibility of Unreported Counterfeits
Sanusi refutes the third objection that miracles might have been countered but the counterfeits were not reported.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of unreported counterfeits cannot undermine the proof of prophethood through miracles.

Core Idea
Any successful counterfeit would have been recorded; history proves none succeeded.

Sanusi now tackles a subtle objection: perhaps a miracle was indeed countered, but the counterfeit was suppressed or lost. He dismantles this possibility by appealing to the universal fame of prophets and the tireless efforts of their opponents. If a true counterfeit had occurred, it would have been broadcast with glee. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The third objection lists several scenarios under which a miracle might have been countered without the counterfeits being transmitted. Read through these possibilities.
Note that the objection is speculative, not based on any actual evidence.
2
Examine Sanusi's refutation
Sanusi declares all these possibilities false 'by necessity'. Identify his key evidence: the fame of prophets and the eagerness of enemies to disprove them.
'By necessity' means the truth is self-evident once the evidence is laid out.
3
Analyze the historical example
Sanusi mentions Musaylima's absurd attempts to counter the Quran. Why does this example strengthen his argument?
Even failed counterfeits were transmitted; a successful one would have been even more notorious.
4
Understand the final point about challengers
Sanusi argues that the opponents of each prophet were the most motivated and capable of countering the miracle. Their failure is itself a proof.
This connects to the idea that miracles are suited to the expertise of the time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : يحتمل أن يكونَ ذلك الأمرُ ممَّا يُعارَضُ : إلا أنه لم يُعارَض لعدم بلوغِهِ إِلى مَنْ يقدرُ على المعارضة ، أو لمواضعة مِنَ القومِ وموافقة في إعلاء كلمته ، أو لخوف ، أو لاستسهال وقلة مبالاة ، أو لاشتغال بما هو أهم ، أو عُورِضَ ولم يُنقَلْ لمانع
وجوابه : أَنَّ جميعَ ما ذُكِرَ باطل معلوم بطلانه بالضرورة ؛ لشهرة أمرِ الرُّسُلِ ، وبلوغه جميع المشارق والمغارب ، ووقوع اهتبال كثيرٍ مِنْ أعداء الدينِ بالقَدْحِ في حُجَجهم بأقصى ما يقدرون عليه ، فلم ينقلبوا إلا خائبين ، وانقاد كثير منهم للحقِّ وأسلم لما ظهر له ؛ كسحرة فرعون وأمثالهم .
ومَنْ وقع منه شيءٌ مِنَ المعارضة اعتنى الخَلْقُ بنقلِهِ ، حتى إنَّهم وَصَّلوا إلينا - ونحنُ في آخرِ الزمانِ ، في آخرِ القرن التاسع ـ ما وقعَ مِنْ تُرَهاتِ مُسَيْلِمَةَ الكذَّابِ لعنه الله تعالى ، التي قصد بها معارضة القرآن العزيز ووَصَّلوا إلينا غير ذلكَ ممَّا ظهرَتْ بهِ فضيحةُ مَنْ سعى في شيءٍ مِنْ ذلكَ والمتحدّونَ في زمانِ كلَّ نبي هم أحقُّ بالمعارضة له في معجزته لو أمكن ذلكَ منهم ؛ لكثرة اشتغالهم في كلِّ زمانٍ بما يناسب ما ظهر على ذلك النبي في زمانهم، ولكثرة كلامهم في ذلكَ ، وفَرْطِ اهتمامهم بالمعارضة ، وتوفر دواعي جميعهم عليها
The third: It is possible that that matter is of the kind that could be countered: except that it was not countered due to it not reaching one who is able to counter it, or due to an agreement of the people and their concurrence in elevating his word, or due to fear, or due to taking it lightly and lack of concern, or due to preoccupation with what is more important, or it was countered but not transmitted due to an obstacle.
And its answer: That all that was mentioned is false, its falsehood known necessarily; because of the fame of the affair of the messengers, and its reaching all the easts and wests, and the occurrence of eagerness of many enemies of religion to disparage their proofs with the utmost of what they are able, so they did not turn back except disappointed, and many of them submitted to the truth and accepted Islam for what became clear to him; like the sorcerers of Pharaoh and their likes.
And whoever did something of counteraction, the people took care to transmit it, to the extent that they conveyed to us - and we are at the end of time, at the end of the ninth century - what occurred of the absurdities of Musaylima the liar, may Allah curse him, by which he intended to counter the Mighty Quran, and they conveyed to us other than that, by which became manifest the disgrace of whoever strove in something of that. And the challengers in the time of every prophet are more entitled to counter him in his miracle if that were possible for them; because of their much occupation in every time with what suits what appeared on that prophet in their time, and the abundance of their speech about that, and their extreme concern with counteraction, and the availability of motives for all of them against it.
Source pages p. 454

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes the third objection: that the miracle might have been counterable but for various reasons (lack of a capable opponent, agreement to elevate the prophet, fear, indifference, preoccupation, or if countered, the counterfeits were not transmitted). Sanusi's answer is decisive: all these possibilities are known to be false necessarily because of the fame of the prophets and the spread of their message everywhere. The enemies of religion eagerly sought to disprove the prophets with all their might but failed; many even submitted to the truth. Moreover, any attempt at counteraction was carefully transmitted, even the absurd attempts of Musaylima the liar. The challengers (opponents) in every prophet's time were the most eager to counter the miracle if possible, as they were deeply engaged in the very field of that prophet's miracle (e.g., sorcery for Moses, medicine for Jesus, eloquence for Muhammad). Their intense concern and multitude of motives make it impossible that a successful counterfeit would go unnoticed or untransmitted.

Key Terms
معارضة
شهرة الرسل
اهتبال الأعداء
ترهات مسيلمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That lack of reported counterfeits might be due to suppression, indifference, or failure to transmit.
Correction: Sanusi shows that the fame of prophets and the zealous efforts of enemies to discredit them, combined with the meticulous transmission of even failed counterfeits (like Musaylima's), make it impossible that a successful counterfeit would go unreported.

Checkpoint
Why does Sanusi consider the third objection false?
A) Because prophets were not famous
B) Because enemies were lazy
C) Because the fame of prophets and the eagerness of enemies to disprove them, along with careful transmission of counterfeits, show that any possible counteraction would have been recorded
D) Because no one ever tried to counter a miracle

Key Takeaway
The third objection fails because the historical record shows that any genuine counter-miracle would have been transmitted by eager enemies, yet only failed attempts like Musaylima's are recorded.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt a flicker of doubt about the truth of Islam because you thought maybe miracles could have been faked? What does this lesson reveal about the integrity of your own heart when faced with such doubts? Will you now actively seek to fortify your certainty by studying the historical record, or will you let the doubt linger?
?
If you had been alive during the time of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), would you have been among the eager enemies trying to disprove him, or among those who submitted? What does your current attitude towards studying the proofs of prophethood say about where your allegiance truly lies? Are you willing to honestly examine your own motives?
?
The enemies of the prophets were intensely motivated to counter the miracles, yet they failed. Do you have that same intensity in seeking the truth and defending your faith? Or have you become complacent, relying on blind imitation? What concrete step will you take today to become a more active seeker of certainty?

Miracles Suited to the Dominant Art of Each Era
Sanusi explains the pattern of miracles matching dominant arts and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah gave each prophet a miracle from the field in which his people excelled, and how this maximises the proof of prophethood.

Core Idea
Miracles are not random; they target the people's greatest pride.

Sanusi explains a pattern in prophetic miracles: each miracle is from the type that was the dominant art in that prophet's era. This was not arbitrary but a strategic choice to make the challenge impossible to deny. In this passage, he gives four examples from the prophets Moses, Jesus, David, and Muhammad (peace be upon them all).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Sanusi states the general rule first, then gives examples.
2
Understand the principle
The principle: the miracle comes from the type that dominated the people, they competed in it, and they boasted about it. This is to make the challenge most effective.
3
Observe the examples
Trace the four examples: sorcery for Moses, medicine for Jesus, music for David, eloquence for Muhammad. See the footnote about David's people being known for musical instruments.
Each example is a distinct category.
4
Reflect on the wisdom
Reflect on why this pattern is important for proving prophethood. The inability of the experts to match the miracle shows it is from Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا جُعِلَتْ لكلِّ نبي معجزةٌ مِنْ جنس ما غلب على أهل زمانِهِ وتهالكوا عليه وتفاخروا به ؛ كالسحر في زمان موسى عليه السلام ، والطب في زمانِ عيسى عليه السلام ، والموسيقا في زمن داود عليهِ السلام (۱) ، والفصاحة في زمان سيّدِ الخَلْقِ نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ
(۱) وكان عليه الصلاة والسلام قد اشتهرت بين قومه صناعة الآلات الموسيقية
And for this, a miracle was made for every prophet from the type that dominated the people of his time and upon which they intensely competed and boasted; like sorcery in the time of Moses (peace be upon him), and medicine in the time of Jesus (peace be upon him), and music in the time of David (peace be upon him), and eloquence in the time of the Master of Creation, our Prophet and Master Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace).
(1) And he (peace and blessings be upon him) was such that the craft of musical instruments was famous among his people.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage provides the rational explanation for a key feature of prophetic miracles: each miracle is of the type that was the pinnacle of human achievement in that prophet's era. The reason is that if the miracle comes in a field where the people are already masters, their inability to match it proves its supernatural origin. Sanusi gives examples: sorcery in the time of Moses (Pharaoh's magicians were renowned), medicine in the time of Jesus (Greek medicine was advanced), music in the time of David (the Israelites were known for musical instruments), and eloquence in the time of Muhammad (the Arabs prided themselves on poetry and rhetoric). The footnote adds that the craft of musical instruments was famous among David's people. This strategy ensures that the challenge is most effective and the miracle's divine origin is clear.

Key Terms
معجزة
جنس ما غلب
السحر
الطب
الموسيقا
الفصاحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are arbitrary divine acts.
Correction: Miracles are strategically chosen to match the dominant art of each era to maximise their proof value.

Checkpoint
Why was Moses given the miracle of sorcery?
A) Because sorcery was the only kind of miracle possible
B) Because sorcery was the dominant art in his time and the people were masters of it
C) Because he was a sorcerer himself
D) Because the people did not understand medicine

Key Takeaway
Allah matches each prophet's miracle to the most advanced human skill of his time so that the people's inability to equal it proves its divine origin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is the skill or art in your life that you boast about most? How does the fact that Allah challenged the people of the past with their own pride make you reconsider your own source of confidence? Will you humble yourself before the miracle of the Qur'an today?
?
If you were to face a miracle from the area of your greatest expertise, would you recognize it as from Allah or dismiss it as just an improvement on your own skill? What does your answer reveal about your heart?
?
The people of Moses used sorcery, and Allah sent a miracle that outdid their best. What 'sorcery' in your life—your most advanced talent or knowledge—are you relying on instead of submitting to the Creator? Will you let go of that pride and accept that only Allah is the source of true power?
