The Miracle as Performative Confirmation of Prophethood
Sanusi presents an objection and answer regarding the proof of prophethood through miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a miracle functions as a performative act of confirmation from God, proving the prophethood of the claimant without requiring a prior verbal declaration.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's performative act, not a statement to be verified.

Sanusi addresses a key objection to the proof of prophethood through miracles: that the miracle cannot prove the claimant's truthfulness unless we first prove that God cannot lie. But how can we prove that? Sanusi's answer reveals a profound insight: the miracle itself is God's direct action that confirms the prophet, akin to a performative speech act. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows why the miracle is self-sufficient as a proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
The objection states that the miracle does not necessitate truthfulness unless we first establish that lying is impossible for God. Notice the two prongs: through revelation (circular) and through reason (not conceded). Understand why the opponent thinks this is a problem.
2
Examine Sanusi's answer
Sanusi says the miracle itself gives knowledge of truthfulness by God's confirmation, without needing prior speech. Reflect on the example of a king appointing an agent: the act itself is the confirmation.
3
Understand the performative nature
The passage explains that the miracle is like a performative utterance (insha') rather than an informative one (ikhbar). This means it creates a reality rather than describing one. How does this solve the circularity issue?
4
Connect to tawatur and internal speech
The passage notes that knowledge is obtained by witnesses directly or through tawatur, regardless of one's position on internal speech. This grounds the use of prophetic reports to establish divine attributes. Why is this important?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : بعد تسليم انتفاء الاحتمالات السابقة كلها ، وكون المعجزة بمنزلة صريح القولِ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى بأنَّ مُدَّعي النبوَّة صادق .. فهو لا يُوجِبُ صدقَهُ إلا بعد استحالةِ الكذب في إخباره تعالى : فلا سبيل إلى ذلكَ بدليل السمع ؛ للزومِ الدورِ ، ولا بدليل العقل ؛ لأنَّ غايتَهُ أنَّ الكذب قبيح ، وهو على الله تعالى مستحيل ، وقبح الكذب عقلاً غيرُ مُسلَّم على أصلكم
وجوابُهُ : أَنَّ مُجرَّدَ ظهورِ المعجزة على يدِهِ يفيدنا العلمَ بِصِدْقِهِ بتصديق الله تعالى إيَّاهُ مِنْ غيرِ افتقار إلى اعتبار كلام وإخبار ، ولهذا يعلمُ صِدْقَ مُدَّعي رسالةِ الملكِ لهُ في المثال المفروض ويعلم تصديق الملكِ لهُ . . كلُّ مَنْ حضرَ ذلكَ المجلس ، أو غابَ عنهُ ووصلَهُ أَمرُهُ بالتواتر ، سواء كانَ ممَّنْ يقولُ بالكلام النفسي ، أو كان لا يقولُ بهِ ومن هنا يصحُ التمسُّكُ بخبر النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في إثباتِ الكلامِ وامتناع الكذب والنقص على الله تعالى ، وإلى هذا يشيرُ ما قالَ إمام الحرمين (١) : إنَّا نجعلُ إظهار المعجزة تصديقاً ، بمنزلة أن يقول : جعلته رسولاً ، وأنشأتُ الرسالة فيه ؛ كقولك : جعلتُكَ وكيلاً ، واستَنَبْتُكَ لشأني مِنْ غيرِ قصدِ إلى إخبار وإعلام بما يثبتُ ومحصولُهُ : أَنَّهُ يُعتبرُ القولُ فيهِ المدلول عليه بالمعجزة إنشاء لا إخباراً .
(١) نقله عنه العلامة السعد بالمعنى في شرح المقاصد » ( ٢/ ١٧٩ ) ، وهو في الإرشاد » ( ص ۳۳۲ )
٤٥٨
وأما لو تم لنا نفي الكذب عنه تعالى بالدليل العقلي مِنْ غيرِ إخبار النبيِّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ . . فلا إشكال حينَئِذٍ (١) .
The fifth: after conceding the negation of all previous probabilities, and that the miracle is in the position of explicit speech from God Almighty that the claimant of prophethood is truthful... it does not necessitate his truthfulness except after the impossibility of lying in His information. So there is no way to that by transmitted evidence due to circularity, nor by rational evidence because its conclusion is that lying is bad, and it is impossible for God Almighty, and the rational badness of lying is not conceded according to your school. And its answer: that mere appearance of the miracle at his hand gives us knowledge of his truthfulness by God Almighty's confirming him, without need to consider speech and information. Therefore, the truthfulness of the claimant of the king's message in the hypothetical example is known, and the king's confirmation of him is known. Everyone who attended that gathering, or was absent and his matter reached him through tawatur, whether he holds to internal speech or not, and from here it is valid to rely on the Prophet's report in establishing speech and the impossibility of lying and deficiency on God Almighty. And to this points what Imam al-Haramayn said: We make the manifestation of the miracle a confirmation, in the position of saying: I have made him a messenger, and I have instituted the message in him; like your saying: I have made you an agent, and I have appointed you for my affair without intending to inform and notify. And its summary: that the statement in it indicated by the miracle is considered as a performative utterance, not an informative one. (1) Quoted from him by al-Sa'd with meaning in Sharh al-Maqasid (2/179), and it is in al-Irshad (p. 332). 458 And as for if we had established the negation of lying from Him Almighty by rational proof without the Prophet's report... then there is no problem then (1).
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and its answer regarding how a miracle proves the truthfulness of a claimant of prophethood. The opponent argues that the miracle does not necessitate truthfulness unless we first establish that lying is impossible for God — which cannot be proven by revelation (circular) nor by reason (since rational badness of lying is not conceded to your school). The answer is that the miracle itself, as a direct act of God, serves as a performative confirmation (insha') rather than an informative statement (ikhbar). It is like God saying 'I have made him a messenger' without needing a prior verbal declaration. Thus anyone who witnesses the miracle or receives the report through tawatur knows the claimant's truthfulness directly, regardless of their position on internal speech. This justifies using the Prophet's report to establish attributes like speech and the impossibility of lying. The passage concludes that if a rational proof for God's truthfulness were established, there would be no issue, but the miracle itself suffices as a performative act.

تصديق
إنشاء
إخبار

تواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That a miracle cannot prove prophethood unless we first establish by reason or revelation that God cannot lie.
Correction: The miracle itself is God's performative act of confirmation, directly proving the prophet's truthfulness without needing prior verification.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does a miracle prove the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood?
A) By being a rational proof that lying is impossible for God
B) By being a performative act of confirmation from God without needing prior speech
C) By being a miracle that exceeds human power
D) By being accompanied by a verbal statement

Key Takeaway
A miracle is God's performative confirmation of the prophet, not a statement that requires prior verification.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the miracles of the Prophet ﷺ, do you accept them as God's direct and sufficient confirmation, or do you find yourself secretly demanding more rational proofs? What does that reveal about your heart's trust in Allah's decisive actions?
?
The miracle is compared to a king saying 'I have made you an agent'—an immediate appointment. In your daily life, do you treat the Prophet's message as a living, present command from Allah, or as a historical report? How would your obedience change if you felt the weight of that direct divine 'yes' behind every miracle?
?
If the miracle is a performative act, not just information, then your response to it is a response to Allah Himself. Are you responding with the obedience and love that such a direct call demands, or have you become desensitized to the urgency of prophethood? What one step will you take today to honor that divine confirmation?

Prophethood

Other Ways to Prove Prophethood Besides Miracles
Sanusi reconciles alternative proofs of prophethood with the primacy of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophethood can be established through means other than miracles, such as necessary knowledge and trustworthy reports, and how this complements the standard miracle-based proof.

Core Idea
Prophethood is proven not only by miracles but also by necessary knowledge and infallible testimony.

Sanusi presents an important clarification: while miracles are the primary proof of prophethood, they are not the only one. Citing al-Maqasid, he shows how necessary knowledge (like Abu Bakr's immediate certainty) and reports from earlier prophets (like those in the Torah and Gospel) also establish prophethood. He then reconciles this with Imam al-Haramayn's claim that only miracles serve as absolute proof, explaining that other proofs are valid but context-dependent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: an admonition, then two methods, then reconciliation, then a note on character.
The passage is dense; read carefully.
2
Identify the two alternative proofs
The passage mentions two ways to prove prophethood besides miracles: necessary knowledge (like Abu Bakr's) and reports from infallible individuals (like Torah and Gospel prophecies). Find these in the text.
These are examples, not an exhaustive list.
3
Understand the reconciliation with Juwayni
Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) claimed only miracles can prove prophethood. Sanusi explains that this applies to absolute proofs for all prophets, but other proofs are valid when context permits.
The phrase 'carried on what is valid as proof absolutely' is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه
1 على طُرُقِ أُخرى في إثباتِ النبوَّة غير المعجزة ]
قال في «المقاصدِ » : ( لا خفاءَ في ثبوتِ النبوَّةِ بخَلْقِ العلم الضروري ؛ كعلم الصدِّيقِ رضيَ الله تعالى عنه ، أو بخبرٍ مَنْ ثبَتَتْ عصمتُهُ مِنَ الكذب ؛ كنصوص التوراة والإنجيل في نبوَّة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وكإخبار موسى عليه الصلاة والسلام بنبوة هارونَ ويُوشع عليهما الصلاة والسلام .
فما ذكرَهُ إمام الحرمين مِنْ أنَّه لا يمكنُ نَصْبُ دليل على النبوَّة سوى المعجزة ؛ لأنَّ ما يُقَدَّرُ دليلاً إنْ لم يكن خارقاً للعادة ، أو خارقاً ولم يكن مقروناً بالدعوى لم يصلح دليلاً ؛ للاتفاق على جواز وقوع الخارقِ مِنَ اللهِ تعالى ابتداءً . . محمول على ما يصلح دليلاً للنبوَّة على الإطلاقِ ، وحُجَّةً على المنكرينَ بالنسبة لكل نبي عليه الصلاة والسلام ، حتى الذي لا نبي قبله ولا كتاب .
وأما ما سيأتي مِنَ الاستدلال على نبوة نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلَّمَ بما شاعَ مِنْ أخلاقه وأحواله.. فعائد إلى المعجزة
Admonition
[On other ways in proving prophethood besides the miracle]
He said in al-Maqasid: 'There is no concealment in the establishment of prophethood by the creation of necessary knowledge, like the knowledge of al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him, or by the report of one whose infallibility from lying is established, like the texts of the Torah and the Gospel regarding the prophethood of our Prophet and master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, and like the informing of Moses, peace be upon him, of the prophethood of Aaron and Joshua, peace be upon them.'
So what Imam al-Haramayn mentioned—that it is not possible to set up a proof for prophethood except the miracle, because whatever is considered a proof, if it is not miraculous, or if it is miraculous but not accompanied by the claim, it is not valid as a proof, due to agreement on the permissibility of the occurrence of a miracle from God, may He be exalted, initially—is carried on what is valid as a proof for prophethood absolutely, and as an argument against deniers with respect to every prophet, peace be upon him, even one before whom there was no prophet nor book.
And as for what will come of the inference to the prophethood of our Prophet and master Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, based on his widespread morals and states, it returns to the miracle.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage discusses alternative ways to prove prophethood besides miracles, citing al-Maqasid. It mentions two: necessary knowledge (like Abu Bakr's immediate certainty) and trustworthy reports from previous scriptures (like Torah and Gospel foretelling Muhammad, and Moses' announcement of Aaron and Joshua). It then reconciles the statement of Imam al-Haramayn (al-Juwayni) that only miracles can serve as proof, clarifying that this applies to absolute proof against all deniers for every prophet, especially those without prior revelation. However, other signs like the Prophet's character, though not independent proofs, ultimately point to the miraculous nature of his message.

Key Terms
النبوّة
المعجزة
العلم الضروري
العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That prophethood cannot be proven except by miracles
Correction: The passage shows other valid methods such as necessary knowledge and reports from earlier prophets, though miracles remain the universal proof.

Checkpoint
According to al-Maqasid, how can prophethood be established besides miracles?
A) Only by miracles
B) By necessary knowledge or reports of infallible individuals
C) By dreams
D) By philosophical deduction

Key Takeaway
Prophethood can be proven through necessary knowledge and infallible reports, in addition to miracles, though miracles remain the universal proof.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Bakr al-Siddiq was certain of the Prophet's truthfulness immediately and without a miracle. When you examine your own heart, is your conviction about prophethood based on such necessary knowledge, or does it rely on external proofs? What might be missing?
?
The passage says earlier scriptures testify to Muhammad's prophethood. Have you ever personally engaged with those texts to strengthen your faith? If not, what is stopping you from seeking that deep certainty?
?
Imagine you are faced with a skeptic who demands a miracle to believe. Your own faith might not be based on a witnessed miracle. Does that unsettle you, or does it drive you to seek the kind of inner certainty that al-Siddiq possessed? Commit to one specific step to move from intellectual assent to that level of conviction.
